Functional and motion behavior notes
- All Small Wooden Blocks are static structural blocks forming deck (top chord/roadway) and bottom chords (tension members).
- All Braces are functional structural connectors (hinge-type links, no volume). They provide:
  • Side-truss braces (Blocks 110–147): alternating diagonals per panel (Warren truss) plus end verticals tying top and bottom chords.
  • Bottom cross-braces (Blocks 148–157): couple bottom chords across x to resist torsion.
  • Top cross-braces (Blocks 158–163): tie deck edge rows across x for lateral stiffness at deck level.
- No Powered Wheels, Torches, or Water Cannons used.

Position adjustment notes
- Corrected right end vertical and top cross-brace endpoints to the y=+8 and y=+10 east deck blocks (Blocks 56 and 58, respectively) to maintain symmetry and exact y alignment. No functional changes.

# builder (gpt-5) (ThoughtEvent): 

Tooling overview and how we’ll use them step by step

- functions.start
  • Purpose: Create and place the very first base block to begin the build.
  • Inputs: init_shift [x, y, z] to position the base; init_rotation [yaw, pitch, roll] if orientation matters; note to describe intent.
  • What I need from you: Desired base position/orientation and conceptual note. In your blueprint, the base origin is at [0, 0, 5.5], which I will use.
  • Tip: The note field is very important and useful as a powerful identifier to record the specific function of this block (e.g., “Default Base Block (stone) – deck center reference”).

- functions.attach_block_to
  • Purpose: Attach a new block directly onto a labeled face of an existing block.
  • Inputs: base_block (ID), face (capitalized face label), new_block (type: Small Wooden Block, Powered Wheel, Torch, Water Cannon), note.
  • What I need: The source block ID and the exact face to use, plus the block type and conceptual note.
  • Tip: The note argument is critical for tracking each block’s role (e.g., “deck x=0,y=+1,z=5.5 – north face of Block 0”).

- functions.connect_blocks
  • Purpose: Place a connector (Brace or Winch) between specific faces of two blocks.
  • Inputs: block_a, face_a, block_b, face_b, connector (Brace/Winch), note.
  • What I need: The two endpoint block IDs and the faces to connect, the connector type, and conceptual note.
  • Constraints: Will fail if faces are too close. We’ll query face details with get_block_details if needed.
  • Tip: The note argument is essential to label structural behavior (e.g., “left diagonal k=-9 – structural hinge diagonal”).

- functions.get_block_details
  • Purpose: Inspect a specific block’s position, rotation, and attachable face details.
  • Inputs: block_id.
  • What I need: The block ID.
  • Use case: Verify face names and alignment prior to attachments or connectors.

- functions.twist_block
  • Purpose: Twist a block around its rooted surface to change pointing direction (angle in degrees).
  • Inputs: block_id, angle.
  • Use case: If any pointer-like block needs reorientation. Likely not needed for Small Wooden Block deck units, but available.

- functions.shift_block
  • Purpose: Fine positional adjustment of an already attached block within [-0.5, 0.5] per axis.
  • Inputs: block_id, shift_real [x, y, z].
  • Use case: If overlap prevents a connection or we need precision alignment.

- functions.flip_spin
  • Purpose: Flip spin direction on blocks that have rotation behavior.
  • Inputs: block_id.
  • Use case: Likely not needed here since your design uses static blocks and braces.

- functions.remove_block
  • Purpose: Remove a block from the machine.
  • Inputs: block_id.
  • Use case: If a placement needs to be undone.

- functions.reset
  • Purpose: Clear the entire build to its initial, empty state.
  • Inputs: none.
  • Use case: Start over if necessary.

- functions.get_machine_summary
  • Purpose: Retrieve the current overview of the machine (without face captions).
  • Inputs: none.
  • Important: We must use this tool for a final check before concluding the build phase of this session, and I will remind you at that time.

Build plan based on your blueprint
1) Start the base at [0, 0, 5.5].
2) Build center deck lane north (Blocks 1–11) and south (Blocks 12–23).
3) Build west deck lane (Blocks 24–35 north; Blocks 36–47 south).
4) Build east deck lane (Blocks 48–59 north; Blocks 60–71 south).
5) Build bottom chord anchor stacks at y = -9 (Blocks 72–75).
6) Build bottom chords x = -1 (Blocks 76–92) and x = +1 (Blocks 93–109).
7) Add left-side Warren truss braces and end verticals (Blocks 110–128).
8) Add right-side Warren truss braces and end verticals (Blocks 129–147).
9) Add bottom cross-bracing across x (Blocks 148–157).
10) Add top cross-bracing across x (Blocks 158–163).
11) Perform a final get_machine_summary to verify.

I will proceed strictly one block operation per step and include informative notes on each block/connection.

Starting with Block 0 now.
